<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer13901236890121561119">As a boy, writer Jay Mackintosh spent three golden summers in the ramshackle home of "Jackapple Joe" Cox. A lonely child, he found solace in Old Joe's simple wisdom and folk charms. The magic was lost, however, when Joe disappeared without warning one fall.<br /><br />Years later, Jay's life is stalled with regret and ennui. His bestselling novel, <em>Jackapple Joe,</em> was published ten year</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13901236890121561119">As a boy, writer Jay Mackintosh spent three golden summers in the ramshackle home of "Jackapple Joe" Cox. A lonely child, he found solace in Old Joe's simple wisdom and folk charms. The magic was lost, however, when Joe disappeared without warning one fall.<br /><br />Years later, Jay's life is stalled with regret and ennui. His bestselling novel, <em>Jackapple Joe,</em> was published ten years earlier and he has written nothing since. Impulsively, he decides to leave his urban life in London and, sight unseen, purchases a farmhouse in the remote French village of Lansquenet. There, in that strange and yet strangely familiar place, Jay hopes to re-create the magic of those golden childhood summers. And while the spirit of Joe is calling to him, it is actually a similarly haunted, reclusive woman who will ultimately help Jay find himself again.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13901236890121561119">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_566941277">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/566941277" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/18383778-dolors" class="left imgcol" title="Dolors"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1379500437p2/18383778.jpg" alt="Dolors" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/566941277?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 21, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/18383778-dolors" class="user" title="Dolors">Dolors</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/18383778-dolors?shelf=read-in-2011" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer566941277">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15401580591622872115">My first novel by the author of Chocolat and I have to say I enjoyed it far more than expected.<br /><br />The story of Jay Mackintosh, a 37 years old writer, famous because of an only novel written fifteen years ago. Jay seems to have lost inspiration and faith in the magic of life, as if all these feelings had been spent in that successful novel.<br />The novel moves forward and backwards in time, and the reader is able to know young Jay, when he meets Joe, an eccentric old man who leaves a deep impression in l</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15401580591622872115">My first novel by the author of Chocolat and I have to say I enjoyed it far more than expected.<br /><br />The story of Jay Mackintosh, a 37 years old writer, famous because of an only novel written fifteen years ago. Jay seems to have lost inspiration and faith in the magic of life, as if all these feelings had been spent in that successful novel.<br />The novel moves forward and backwards in time, and the reader is able to know young Jay, when he meets Joe, an eccentric old man who leaves a deep impression in lonely Jay, becoming his special friend and his secret hideaway.<br />Home brewed wine made by Joe takes unusual importance in the present time of the story, because it's only when Jay drinks it that he finds the courage to change what makes him unhappy. Guided by a kind of Joe's ghost, Jay leaves London and moves to a little rural village in France where he buys an abandoned farm and where he starts writing again, inspired by his mysterious neighbour, Marisa.<br /><br />This is a book about haunted lives, unfinished stories and the chance to change your own life and atone for your past mistakes.<br />Magic, wine, faith or simply luck and coincidence. Choose your own explanation.<br />I'll stick to the magic and a bit of luck, as Jay says.<br />It's only a matter of not losing hope completely and let others surprise you, with one foot in the Earth and the other one suspended in the air, letting the wind blow where it has to.<br /><br />Refreshing, heartening and uplifting reading. Great for dreamers and romantics.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15401580591622872115">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_67326605">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/67326605" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/223837-nikki" class="left imgcol" title="Nikki"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1308224598p2/223837.jpg" alt="Nikki" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/67326605?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 03, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/223837-nikki" class="user" title="Nikki">Nikki</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/223837-nikki?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/223837-nikki?shelf=contemporary" class="actionLinkLite">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer67326605">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17582013936062001732">The first time I tried to read Blackberry Wine apparently wasn't the <em>right</em> time to try to read this book. This time, though, I read it practically all in one go -- with, yeah, a glass of wine. Joanne Harris' prose is always easy to read, really clear, and I can believe in the characters she creates at least enough to carry on to the very last page. Joe, in particular, rang true with me: a miner's son, a gardener, a Yorkshire lad... Jay, perhaps not as much, particularly not at the beginning, but</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17582013936062001732">The first time I tried to read Blackberry Wine apparently wasn't the <em>right</em> time to try to read this book. This time, though, I read it practically all in one go -- with, yeah, a glass of wine. Joanne Harris' prose is always easy to read, really clear, and I can believe in the characters she creates at least enough to carry on to the very last page. Joe, in particular, rang true with me: a miner's son, a gardener, a Yorkshire lad... Jay, perhaps not as much, particularly not at the beginning, but yes, enough that I cared what happened to him.<br /><br />I love the everyday magic that Joanne Harris' characters work. Just normal enough that you can believe it's true for a while. Just close enough to coincidence or wishful thinking that if you can't step over into fantasy, you don't have to.<br /><br />I don't think I'm likely to reread any of Joanne Harris' books: I guess to me they're a bit like chocolate, or a bottle of wine. You can only have the experience once. But I do greatly enjoy them, and will be sad when there are no more that I can read.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17582013936062001732">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1437127978">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1635134430437873339"> I loved this story, or maybe I should say, I was in love with this story, I was in love with Joe and his eccentric ways. I loved the gardening, the wine making, the magic. I was in love with the bond of love between old man Joe and young man Jay. This is a book about the young man growing into maturity, into a man who can love a woman and a child and protect what he values. Growing into a man who can accept the weaknesses and mistakes of others, accept those same things in himself, and figure o</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1635134430437873339"> I loved this story, or maybe I should say, I was in love with this story, I was in love with Joe and his eccentric ways. I loved the gardening, the wine making, the magic. I was in love with the bond of love between old man Joe and young man Jay. This is a book about the young man growing into maturity, into a man who can love a woman and a child and protect what he values. Growing into a man who can accept the weaknesses and mistakes of others, accept those same things in himself, and figure out how to make things better. It is about an old man passing on his skills and dreams to the next generation. It is about the value of the past to the creation of the future; respect and love for the land and diversity of species. Although the story has many fantastical elements the only thing that struck a somewhat odd note for me was Marise's past. Lovely woman, but more than her share of conveniently dead in her life and rather iffy taste in men, although let's hope that we are looking at a brighter future for her. Truly, I just loved this book. For me, it was better than Chocolat and better than Five Quarters of an Orange. I don't drink wine but I related absolutely to the wine in this story; to the stories it tells, to the stories it releases. Sometimes I want to hug a book. This is one of those books. I haven't yet looked to see how others liked this book, but I recommend it. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1635134430437873339">...more</a>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16728696401027929498">This is a beautiful book, written by the author who later wrote Chocolat. Blackberry Wine takes place in both England and the same small French town that is the setting for Chocolat.<br /><br />Blackberry Wine tells the story of Jay, who as a boy, meets an eccentric man named Joe, who opens Jay's world to gardening and magic and homemade wine. <div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_298529364">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/298529364" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5092701-chris-eastvedt" class="left imgcol" title="Chris Eastvedt"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442535376p2/5092701.jpg" alt="Chris Eastvedt" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/298529364?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 21, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5092701-chris-eastvedt" class="user" title="Chris Eastvedt">Chris Eastvedt</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5092701-chris-eastvedt?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer298529364">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6432974958382827657">I prefer tea….<br /><br />I have mixed feelings about Blackberry Wine, unfortunately more negative than positive. For the first ten chapters I despised this book: I didn’t care about the characters, couldn’t care about the plot and wanted nothing more than to just get through the thing so I could move on to another story. Even though the chapters are short, fifty-seven pages is more than I want to wait for a story to get interesting.<br /><br />Blackberry Wine describes the life of Jay, a one-hit-wonder in the literary</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6432974958382827657">I prefer tea….<br /><br />I have mixed feelings about Blackberry Wine, unfortunately more negative than positive. For the first ten chapters I despised this book: I didn’t care about the characters, couldn’t care about the plot and wanted nothing more than to just get through the thing so I could move on to another story. Even though the chapters are short, fifty-seven pages is more than I want to wait for a story to get interesting.<br /><br />Blackberry Wine describes the life of Jay, a one-hit-wonder in the literary arena who fell victim to the freshman curse and now lives as a writer of trashy sci-fi novels and part-time fantasy-conference attendee. One day he impulsively buys a farmhouse in France that brings back childhood memories and moves in, hoping to find what he thinks he’s lost. Via astral projection, his friend/mentor Joe, visits the farmhouse to continue giving the advice he started in Jay’s youth. Jay the adult reverts back to the child he was time and again in his bitterness at being abandoned by the old man’s sudden parting, continuing the legacy. Blackberry Wine is written as a piece of commercial fiction, but has definite elements of fantasy that feel out of place. This inconsistent tone added to my discomfort.<br /><br />One of the reasons I had trouble with this book is because of the way Jay is written. Personally, I thought he was schizophrenic, but I don’t think that was the author’s intention. He seems like an intelligent person, but has the insight of a fifteen-year-old boy coupled with a dog’s manic need to defend his territory (or in this case, Jay’s righteous indignation). Jay’s lack of maturity and poor decision-making ability mark him as a victim, a martyr, so I had trouble caring about him.<br /><br />This book jumps back and forth in time about every other chapter which I found distracting. The copious descriptions were a bit much and repetitive: how many times did I have to hear about the canal, or that something was yeasty- an odd word to be given such prominence? And don’t get me started on the magically animated bottles of wine….<br /><br />On the upside, once the story warmed up it was engaging. Jay’s garden renovation and the relationship with his neighbor and her daughter were nice, the practical peculiarities of Joe added color and interest and the French townspeople formed a nice backdrop. All in all I thought Blackberry Wine was flawed, but it did have moments.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6432974958382827657">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/20753314?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 24, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1107216-holli" class="user" title="Holli">Holli</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer20753314">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9195436565241064362">I really enjoyed this. I liked the setting (England and France) and the magical quality of the story. I liked the old character, Joe and in my mind saw one of our library patrons playing his part. It made me want to read more of Harris's books. I like the way she conveys that there is more going on in our lives than meets the eye.<br /><br />From Publishers Weekly<br />Like her well-received 1999 novel, Chocolat, Harris's latest outing unfolds around the arrival of an outsider in a tiny French town. This time win</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9195436565241064362">I really enjoyed this. I liked the setting (England and France) and the magical quality of the story. I liked the old character, Joe and in my mind saw one of our library patrons playing his part. It made me want to read more of Harris's books. I like the way she conveys that there is more going on in our lives than meets the eye.<br /><br />From Publishers Weekly<br />Like her well-received 1999 novel, Chocolat, Harris's latest outing unfolds around the arrival of an outsider in a tiny French town. This time wine replaces chocolate as Harris's magic elixir, and the newcomer to the village of Lansquenet sur Tannes is Jay Mackintosh, a 37-year-old has-been writer from London. Fourteen years have passed since Jay's debut novel, Jackapple Joe, won the Prix Goncourt. Since then, he has been churning out B-novels under a pseudonym; he currently lives with his girlfriend, Kerry, an aggressively successful 25-year-old celebrity journalist. Flashbacks reveal that Jay's only recollections of happiness are the golden summers he spent as a youth with old Joseph "Jackapple Joe" Cox in the small English town of Kirby Monckton. Joe, a colorful character who made wines from fruits and berries, inspired Joe's successful first novel. But one day he disappeared. When Jay stumbles across an advertisement for an 18th-century "chateau" in wine-growing country, the spell of his misery is broken. After downing a bottle of Joe's '75 Special, which he has been hoarding for 24 years, Jay decides to buy the house sight unseen. Leaving Kerry in London, Jay moves to Lansquenet and starts a new rural life, beginning to write under his own name again. He is bewildered by his reclusive neighbor, Marise d'Api, who apparently coveted his derelict house and land, and is ostracized by the townspeople. Jay's quest to discover why everyone, including Marise's former mother-in-law, blames Marise for her husband's suicide keeps the plot moving at a steady clip. Despite some unbelievable twists and a slightly uneven paceAit begins slowly, but by the last quarter races aheadAthis is an entertaining narrative, equal parts whimsy and drama. (July) </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9195436565241064362">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a href="/review/list/2513987-janice?shelf=love-the-cover" class="actionLinkLite">love-the-cover</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1034499827">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5932296672528966926">When I compare this offering from Joanne Harris to her other books, it is just a meh response. I was disappointed. <br /><br />It flipped back and forth between 1975 and 1999 too rapidly. I couldn't really get into either period. The ending was abrupt, like the author herself was tired of the whole thing.<br /><br />I did like some of the characters - Joe &amp; Rosa. It was nice to be in the company of Josephine and Roux again. And there was lots of wine and food to be enjoyed.<br /><br /></span>

          </span>

  <a href="/user/show/10549695-margaret" class="left imgcol" title="Margaret"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1390960671p2/10549695.jpg" alt="Margaret" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/613836322?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 13, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/10549695-margaret" class="user" title="Margaret">Margaret</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer613836322">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11208322058663841242">Of all the books written by Harris, this is my favorite by far. It is a delightful tale of young Jay MacIntosh and the friendship he develops with Joe Cox over the course of 3 summers spent at a small village in England. Joe's past is never made clear; his tales become truth and his truths become tales. The one certainty is that Joe, in his ramshackle cabin knows all there is to know about gardening, herbs and their "magical" healing and protective powers, and wine-making. Althouogh the quality</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11208322058663841242">Of all the books written by Harris, this is my favorite by far. It is a delightful tale of young Jay MacIntosh and the friendship he develops with Joe Cox over the course of 3 summers spent at a small village in England. Joe's past is never made clear; his tales become truth and his truths become tales. The one certainty is that Joe, in his ramshackle cabin knows all there is to know about gardening, herbs and their "magical" healing and protective powers, and wine-making. Althouogh the quality of the wine could be debated. After Jay's parents divorce and he is sent back to school in London, his unhappiness is so great that he decides to return to Joe; only to find Joe has vanished without a good-bye.<br />Jay grows up to write one acclaimed novel based on Joe Cox, his childhood friend, but no more great writing comes to him. When Jay sees a picture of a farmhouse in Lansquenet, France, he is reminded of Joe's dream of one day owning such a place. On sudden impulse, Jay buys the property without seeing it first, packs a duffle bag, his typewriter and a few bottles of wine he managed to retrieve from Joe's abandoned home and leaves his urban London life to farm and to write another novel.<br />I loved the few references to Vianne and Roux (Chocolat); I also loved the fact that while a strong woman character enters the story, this is the story of Jay, a male character who is struggling to find himself and to put his friendship with Joe into perspective without the feeling of betrayal at not being able to say good-bye. There is still magic and whimsy, but it is without the darkness of the controversy between magic and the church. Finally, I loved the fact that Jay does write his next great novel with surprising results, and that he does win the struggle of finding out just what he has been searching for over the years. Oh! One more thing....the references to so many of the great songs in the 70's was a delightful, whimsical touch, no magic needed, that made me smile. (Springsteen, Beach Boys, Elvis...)_</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11208322058663841242">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer720149079475757815">I read this book as a recommendation from my monthly book club. As someone who might be described as enjoying a glass of wine (perhaps two..), I was looking forward to reading it. I thoroughly enjoyed it. I loved the characters, the tiny town in France, the bottles of wine that "spoke" (I could relate to that), to Jay and to the belief that all good things can come from a little magic. Because I so enjoyed the movie Chocolat (I had not read the book), I went into this book thinking that it would</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText720149079475757815">I read this book as a recommendation from my monthly book club. As someone who might be described as enjoying a glass of wine (perhaps two..), I was looking forward to reading it. I thoroughly enjoyed it. I loved the characters, the tiny town in France, the bottles of wine that "spoke" (I could relate to that), to Jay and to the belief that all good things can come from a little magic. Because I so enjoyed the movie Chocolat (I had not read the book), I went into this book thinking that it would have the same kind of magic/mystery about it. I was not disappointed. When you read this book, you won't be either!</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1362919989">

  <a href="/user/show/5204784-vonia" class="left imgcol" title="Vonia"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1445761806p2/5204784.jpg" alt="Vonia" /></a>

      <a href="/user/show/5204784-vonia" class="user" title="Vonia">Vonia</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7426094-blackberry-wine" title="Paperback " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=magical-realism" class="actionLinkLite">magical-realism</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=ghosts-gothic-spiritual" class="actionLinkLite">ghosts-gothic-spiritual</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=grief-death" class="actionLinkLite">grief-death</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=french" class="actionLinkLite">french</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=sweet-reads" class="actionLinkLite">sweet-reads</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=motherhood" class="actionLinkLite">motherhood</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=friendships" class="actionLinkLite">friendships</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=books-about-writers" class="actionLinkLite">books-about-writers</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=small-town-lives" class="actionLinkLite">small-town-lives</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=neighbors" class="actionLinkLite">neighbors</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1362919989">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14930274898889679006">I read Harris' Five Quarters of the Orange &amp; Blackberry Wine back to back, so I shalll review them together. They are very similar, actually; a little too much. Both feature lead female protagonists that have strong, proud, independent, walled-away personalities, unwilling to accept, let alone ask, others for any sort of assistance. In both, they are not the lead character, but as the focus of the protagonist, they are as, if not more, important. <br /><br />In Five Quarters of the Orange, this bold fem</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14930274898889679006">I read Harris' Five Quarters of the Orange &amp; Blackberry Wine back to back, so I shalll review them together. They are very similar, actually; a little too much. Both feature lead female protagonists that have strong, proud, independent, walled-away personalities, unwilling to accept, let alone ask, others for any sort of assistance. In both, they are not the lead character, but as the focus of the protagonist, they are as, if not more, important. <br /><br />In Five Quarters of the Orange, this bold female character is Mirabelle Dartigen, the mother of present-day narrator Framboise Simon. <br /><br />In Blackberry Wine, Marise d'Api is the strong female lead, writer Jay Mackintosh's unfriendly, closed off, and mysterious neighbor. <br /><br />Like in all Harris' novels - the singular touch that ensures my return interest in her novels - both novels contain a food that serves as a saving elixir and the irreplaceable addition of magic and whimsy. The former uses an orange, the scent of which inexplicably increases Mirabelle's anxiety spells (for some time, admist verbal and sometimes physical abuse from her, Framboise surreptitiously leaves orange peels to seep through the ventilation so as to earn a reprieve). In the latter, the elixir is fruit-based wine, specifically a set of vintage '75s, which Jay Mackintosh finds in the remains of Pog Hill decades ago when he returns the summer following his unannounced disappearance.<br /><br />Five Quarters of the Orange tells a multi-generational story with lies, secrets, family database, but with redemption, love, healing, and perseverance shining throughout. Framboise, having had a tenuous relationship with her less than ideal mother (abusive, actually) all her life, she is surprised to uncover redeeming secrets written in code in a beloved cookbook that belonged to her. Her childhood took place during the Nazi occupation, causing more than typical difficulties in her young years. Along with her siblings Cassis &amp; Reinette, they begin associating with a German Officer named Leibwitz. For varying reasons, each idolizes, to the point of compromising their integrity by becoming informants, providing information Leibwitz utilizes to blackmail their neighbors. They rationalize this by convincing themselves as well as each other that this is harmless; it is only words, after all, and it isn't like the Germans are murdering anyone. (Although one evening there is one somewhat accidental related death.) <br /><br />Framboise falls the most for Liebwitz. By, in fact, actually falling in love with him. Which leads to the event that has remained hidden for years, decades, in the family. The event that changed each of their lives forever. When he tells young Framboise that he can no longer see her, likely ever again, she cries, imploring that this not be so. When he refuses her pleas, she desperately convinces him to swim out to a dangerous area of the lake, simply to spend more time with him. He is caught in a root underwater and drowns. The three of them, Cassis, Reinette, and Framboise, surreptitiously make the body disappear, and never discuss the incident again. Their mother, despite showing no real love for them their entire lives, covers up for them when she finds out. They never know until present day that she even knew.<br /><br />All these events lead to the entire city shunning the family, and following one situation too many, they flee in separate directions, barely in time escaping death by the neighbors' wrath and need to designate a scapegoat. Of course, there is also the love aspect, a childhood friend, Paul, whom she eventually lets in. Together they learn to heal. If not forget, but to accept the past, their indivual secrets, and Framboise finally makes amends with her mother.<br /><br />Blackberry Wine I liked far less. Jay honestly seemed like an immature adult, left in the past. Worse yet, he is aware of it, yet quite nonchalant to the idea of changing. His personal relationships are minimal, he hardly allows himself aspirations, avoiding any real work. Honestly, none of the other main characters were that much better. His love interest, Marie A'pi, is a negative, closed off person for most of the novel. The ghost of Joe is more lovable, but honestly his presence was perplexing. I am typically a fan of magical realism, but the ghosts/spirituality aspect was not smoothly embedded into the story. it definitely stood out, causing the reading to seem off-kilter. Kerry, his initial love interest, was written like a bitch, clear and simple. All the other characters in the new town, neighbors to Jay, were not very deeply explored. Relatives to Marise (similar to the neighbors in Five Quarters of an Orange) were cold and unwilling to be understanding, believing only what they want to believe.<br /><br />The only character that was well-written for me was his childhood friend during his Pog Hills days. Gilly was courageous, spunky, and had a spirit that was lovable rather than unattractive. Marise's daughter, whom Jay initially mistakes for her, comes close to bringing back the spirit. <br /><br />In all, two fun reads, but I am still searching for a book from Harris in which the depth and overall significance of her words and stories match the way she has perfected the tone of magic and whimsy. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14930274898889679006">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16506565545200540798">Joanne Harris most certainly could never be accused of being stuck in a genre. Her books vary wildly in content and style as does my opinion of them.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText16506565545200540798">Joanne Harris most certainly could never be accused of being stuck in a genre. Her books vary wildly in content and style as does my opinion of them. At one end of the scale sits the outstanding Gentlemen and Players; at the other Blue Eyed Boy which I thought was pretty dire. This one has echoes of Chocolat in its flamboyant descriptions of taste and colour - some of the book even takes place in the same village. A lovely whimsical tale of a young boy, Jay, who spends most of his childhood holidays with Joe, a gardener, who grows rare potatoes and just about everything else in his allotment. A chance advertisement many years later sees Jay leave everything behind to buy a dilapidated house in France. 3.5 but feeling generous.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/46045375?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 25, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1956252-nancy" class="user" title="Nancy">Nancy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1956252-nancy?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1956252-nancy?shelf=books-about-books" class="actionLinkLite">books-about-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1956252-nancy?shelf=england" class="actionLinkLite">england</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer46045375'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer46045375">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8473834980938792055"> This is the fifth Joanne Harris novel I’ve read and what I love about her style of writing is the subtle magic that you’re never quite sure is the character’s imagination or a mystical reality. Then she allows another character in on the ‘vision,’ (in this case the child Rosa) and you just marvel at the whole thing. It’s symbolic of letting go and trusting our feelings.<br /><br />Although her theme here is about the magical properties of a special wine, her underlying message is one of goodness, understan</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8473834980938792055">	This is the fifth Joanne Harris novel I’ve read and what I love about her style of writing is the subtle magic that you’re never quite sure is the character’s imagination or a mystical reality. Then she allows another character in on the ‘vision,’ (in this case the child Rosa) and you just marvel at the whole thing. It’s symbolic of letting go and trusting our feelings.<br /><br />Although her theme here is about the magical properties of a special wine, her underlying message is one of goodness, understanding, appreciating the simple life and relying on one’s own creative resources to lead a satisfactory life. Ironically, her protagonist, Jay Mackintosh, is a writer, as is Harris herself, and yet the lessons he learns from the old man Joe don’t come from writing about him (though it does lead to a successful first book), but by adopting his simple lifestyle. You want to cheer when he rejects the glitz and glamour of fame and celebrity. (I’m putting a spoiler on this review in case I’m revealing too much).<br /><br />In many ways Harris explores the same theme and uses the same techniques of her better known book, “Chocolat.” The modern part of the story takes place in the same small French town and some of the same characters pop in for brief appearances. It’s not repetitive though, I haven’t tired of reading Harris yet—she’s a great writer!<br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_347785829">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/347785829" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4962920-jill-furedy" class="left imgcol" title="Jill Furedy"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1298347877p2/4962920.jpg" alt="Jill Furedy" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/347785829?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 13, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4962920-jill-furedy" class="user" title="Jill Furedy">Jill Furedy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/321573.Blackberry_Wine" title="Hardcover 9780380978724" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer347785829">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3202202939642209393">Unlike Chocolat, these characters couldn't hold their own, which is funny since the book is set near Lansquenet and the charcters from Chocolat hover in the sidelines throughout the story. Josephine and Caro and Georges Clairmont are the main people who interact with Jay, though Roux darts through various scenes as well. But Roux was never as charismatic in the book as he was in the movie, so I didn't mind his non-impact here..though it just seemed like odd name dropping by the author to continu</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3202202939642209393">Unlike Chocolat, these characters couldn't hold their own, which is funny since the book is set near Lansquenet and the charcters from Chocolat hover in the sidelines throughout the story. Josephine and Caro and Georges Clairmont are the main people who interact with Jay, though Roux darts through various scenes as well. But Roux was never as charismatic in the book as he was in the movie, so I didn't mind his non-impact here..though it just seemed like odd name dropping by the author to continually mention his presence.<br /> This book started off slowly, but towards the middle I thought it was picking up and it began to grow on me. Unfortunately, that didn't carry through to the ending. From the beginning Jay is rather unlikeable, he's a blocked writer, churning out books he's not proud of, dating a woman he doesn't care for, and his flashbacks mostly emphasize his sullen, cowardly personality. Joe seems like he might have been interesting had he been a developed character and not just a device to propel Jay forward. Marise was fine as a neighbor, but even as her backstory filled in, she wasn't strong enough to be a lead character much less a love interest. After my disappointment in Vianne and Roux's relationship in Chocolat and again in The Girl With No Shadow, I'm not sure Harris has any interest in building the chemistry necessary to make a compelling love story. Marise's daughter Rosa, also didn't live up to her potential. Her story leads to the only real action in the book, but as the events seem to be leading to an actual climax, it just fizzles out. Jay appears to duck the potential conflict, living up to his cowardice from his youth, and Mireille's story abruptly vanishes. If the ending had been strong, I could have forgiven the lackluster beginning. But the ending was frustrating and the middle wasn't strong enough to hold the whole thing up. Makes me less eager to read another of her books, but I'm still willing to try one more.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3202202939642209393">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_220198545">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/220198545" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5855795-filipe-miguel" class="left imgcol" title="Filipe Miguel"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1372164686p2/5855795.jpg" alt="Filipe Miguel" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/220198545?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 24, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5855795-filipe-miguel" class="user" title="Filipe Miguel">Filipe Miguel</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/3439816-vinho-m-gico" title="Paperback 9789724123981" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5855795-filipe-miguel?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5855795-filipe-miguel?shelf=suspense" class="actionLinkLite">suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer220198545">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16520635532421102820">Não há qualquer dúvida de que gostei do que li, ou não fosse fã confesso da escrita e imaginação da autora, mas pela primeira vez, num livro de Joanne Harris, não senti satisfação do principio ao fim. Aliás, foi precisamente aí, principio e fim, que surgiram as grandes dúvidas.<br /><br />A história começa abruptamente e abruptamente acaba. No espaço de poucas páginas, damos por Jay a tomar uma decisão impulsiva que o leva a abandonar a vida que leva e a lançar-se em algo que ele próprio não sabe o que é. N</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16520635532421102820">Não há qualquer dúvida de que gostei do que li, ou não fosse fã confesso da escrita e imaginação da autora, mas pela primeira vez, num livro de Joanne Harris, não senti satisfação do principio ao fim. Aliás, foi precisamente aí, principio e fim, que surgiram as grandes dúvidas.<br /><br />A história começa abruptamente e abruptamente acaba. No espaço de poucas páginas, damos por Jay a tomar uma decisão impulsiva que o leva a abandonar a vida que leva e a lançar-se em algo que ele próprio não sabe o que é. No final, em pouco mais de três folhas a narrativa é encerrada, quando parecia haver potencial para bastante mais.<br /><br />Pelo meio temos o verdadeiro sumo do livro, a mistura que lhe dá real cor e cheiro. <br /><br />Passado entre meados dos anos 70 e o final do século XX, andamos sucessivamente a saltitar entre Pog Hill Lane em Inglaterra e Lasquenet em França. Seja a acompanhar Jay nas suas peripécias de criança ao lado do transversal-ao-tempo Joe, ou a visitar com ele Lasquenet, todos os momentos são preenchidos e saborosos. <br /><br />Conhecemos personangens "marcantes", como Marise e Rosa, outras não tão marcantes, Zeth e Kerry, mas ficamos com a impressão que podia ter sido servido algo mais delas. Na realidade, sendo verdadeiramente sincero, não considero que cheguem a ser marcantes. Deveriam ter tido mais peso na história e não aparecerem apenas de passagem. No fundo, todos ficaram entregues à condição de acessório e foi passada a ideia de que nada mais importava senão Jay e os seus devaneios Joeísticos.<br /><br />A subida de Jay nas impressões gerais da população de Lasquenet, contudo, é interessante e chegamos a sentir-nos embebidos por toda aquela calma e "fofoquice", tão típicia de lugares pequenos.<br /><br />Quanto a Lasquenet propriamente dita, poderá ser uma qualquer aldeia junto a um rio, com pretensões de crescimento, carregada de nostalgia e com medo desse mesmo desenvolvimento. Pitoresca q.b., com habitantes cliché (facto que não os torna desinteressantes, de forma alguma!), cheia de virtudes e defeitos.<br /><br />Chegados ao fim, ficamos com a sensação que estivemos a ler um livro extremamente bem escrito sobre o quotidiano, que versa sobre a infância, sobre a vida adulta, sobre impulsos, crenças, magia e... sabores, sobre tudo e sobre nada. Talvez lhe falte um pouco de sal. <br /><br />Acabaram-se os Especiais, acabou-se a história!<br /><br />PS - Considero a tradução do titulo do livro mal conseguida, pese embora não destoe do conteúdo. Preferia um Vinho de Amoras ou Vinho de Amoras Silvestres, ao invés deste Vinho Mágico, um tanto ou quanto infantil.<br /><br />Rating: 3.5/5.0</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16520635532421102820">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/233903703?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 29, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3333943-judy" class="user" title="Judy">Judy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">romance readers who like a twist</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3333943-judy?shelf=21st-century-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">21st-century-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3333943-judy?shelf=slipstream" class="actionLinkLite">slipstream</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3333943-judy?shelf=reading-group-pick" class="actionLinkLite">reading-group-pick</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer233903703">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7208136193673382877">This was a reading group pick and I voted for it because I liked the movie "Chocolat" so wanted to read some books by this author. Blackberry Wine is pretty good; a romance made better because she addressed creativity, community, financial greed and a few other issues.<br /><br />Jay Mackintosh is a blocked novelist, living in London with one of those business-like, smart, pushy young women who seem to run the world these days. He wrote one good novel but now can only write trash. Luckily the trash brings h</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7208136193673382877">This was a reading group pick and I voted for it because I liked the movie "Chocolat" so wanted to read some books by this author. Blackberry Wine is pretty good; a romance made better because she addressed creativity, community, financial greed and a few other issues.<br /><br />Jay Mackintosh is a blocked novelist, living in London with one of those business-like, smart, pushy young women who seem to run the world these days. He wrote one good novel but now can only write trash. Luckily the trash brings him good money, so when he spies a real estate brochure for a farmhouse in a remote French village, he can just buy it and move there.<br /><br />Despite the girlfriend, a few troublesome villagers and a mysterious neighbor, Jay's wishes all come true in a year's time. He even finds love.<br /><br />Because this is Joanne Harris, a magical element runs through the story. I do love magic in stories, though I wasn't entirely thrilled by the ways this author employed it. Most surprising was how most of my fellow reading group members did not have a problem with it because they are absolutely NOT fantasy readers.<br /><br />My favorite character was Jay's childhood friend, a gypsy girl named Gilly who helped him man up when he was a wimpy kid. I also liked the French villagers who preferred their tight-knit community and small vineyards to becoming a tourist town in Provence.<br /><br />Joanne Harris has her heart in the right place and I like her whimsical outlook as well as her humor. I found her almost too lightweight but she will be one of those authors I turn to after a stint of the dark, heavy, literary reading I love the best.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7208136193673382877">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_65980615">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/65980615" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2076721-djrmel" class="left imgcol" title="Djrmel"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1289164686p2/2076721.jpg" alt="Djrmel" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/65980615?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 05, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2076721-djrmel" class="user" title="Djrmel">Djrmel</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2076721-djrmel?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2076721-djrmel?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer65980615">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2199316397076815847">Blackberry Wine followed Harris's Chocolat, but well preceeded the movie of Chocolat that brought so many readers to her books. The timing of the writing of these books is relevent, because Blackberry Wine takes place in the same world as Chocolat, with a few characters making cameo appearences. Then came The Lollypop Shoes (or The Girl with No Shadow), a true sequel to Chocolat, and the casting and plot changes from the film are stamped all over the story. But Blackberry Wine continues with the</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2199316397076815847">Blackberry Wine followed Harris's Chocolat, but well preceeded the movie of Chocolat that brought so many readers to her books. The timing of the writing of these books is relevent, because Blackberry Wine takes place in the same world as Chocolat, with a few characters making cameo appearences. Then came The Lollypop Shoes (or The Girl with No Shadow), a true sequel to Chocolat, and the casting and plot changes from the film are stamped all over the story. But Blackberry Wine continues with the light touches of magic and etherealness that made Chocolat such a special book. <br /><br />This time, we have a blocked writter (is there any other kind in novels?) who runs away to re-create the place that gave birth to the one book that he was proud he wrote. Quickly he is immersed in the gossip and real lives of the people of the very special French town that always seems to have a dark secret or two just waiting to be revealed. Yes, it's a novel based on a cliched story, but when the setting and characters have as many layers as a Harris novel, the cliche almost seems new. <br /><br />I am going to nitpic one problem with the story-telling of this book (it might have made 5 stars with me if not for this error): inexplainably, Harris jumps from 3rd person limited narrative to 3rd person omniscent twice in this book, and for just a few short paragraphs. The POV switch glares as something an editor should have caught, and wreak havoc with the flow of the story.<br /><br />Other than that, this is one very, very readable and enjoyable book by an author who really knows how to develop characters. (And for fans of Roux....he's in this one too!)</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_565460856">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/565460856" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1062592-kathleen" class="left imgcol" title="Kathleen"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1391478281p2/1062592.jpg" alt="Kathleen" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/565460856?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 19, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1062592-kathleen" class="user" title="Kathleen">Kathleen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1062592-kathleen?shelf=favorite-contemporary-authors" class="actionLinkLite">favorite-contemporary-authors</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer565460856">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17157581610239293277">Fair warning: I’m on a bit of a Joanne Harris binge these days. ”Blackberry Wine” is the story of a writer, widely acclaimed for an insightful novel written fourteen years earlier and financially solvent from lesser sci-fi writing, who is now stuck on so many levels. <br />The novel alternates between Jay McIntosh’s memories of three summers over twenty years before and the present. Adolescent, lonely, left adrift by his parents’ egocentricity and divorce, Jay finds solace from an eccentric, mysteriou</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17157581610239293277">Fair warning: I’m on a bit of a Joanne Harris binge these days. ”Blackberry Wine” is the story of a writer, widely acclaimed for an insightful novel written fourteen years earlier and financially solvent from lesser sci-fi writing, who is now stuck on so many levels. <br />The novel alternates between Jay McIntosh’s memories of three summers over twenty years before and the present. Adolescent, lonely, left adrift by his parents’ egocentricity and divorce, Jay finds solace from an eccentric, mysterious man whose stories he is not sure he believes. Nevertheless he is mesmerized by them and what the old man can grow on land that would seem unable to sustain any living thing. Over the course of three summers he learns as much as his adolescent personality allows him to understand about living resourcefully, close to the earth, “having a heart,” and a bit of magic. Meeting a fearless young girl who shares his fascination with found objects in Pog Hill and the dark canal nearby, he fills his days with adventure and finds courage sometimes to stand up to the bullies that troll the area. <br />In the present, Jay McIntosh, self-centered, self-pitying, impulsively buys a property in the tiny village of Lansquenet and flees London and his live-in girlfriend carrying six bottles of homemade wine from those summers long ago. Surrounded by many of the characters from “Chocolat” and “Peaches for Father Francis,” he immerses himself into the lives of the villagers, finding another "important" novel to write, rebuilds his farmhouse and land, pays attention to the magic of the six bottles of wine, and finally finds his way. <br />The pull of this novel for me is about the rebuilding of land and heart and the story of Jay’s reclusive neighbor and her daughter, resiliency and fierce love set against the gossip of the village. Jay spends a lot of time in the novel battling anger that I couldn’t always understand its power to blind or mislead him after so many years (I am a believer in the “moveon.com” philosophy), but this is still a rich, sustaining story filled with lush descriptions of the land, the people, and their conversations.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17157581610239293277">...more</a>

          </span>

  <a href="/user/show/117720-lindyloumac" class="left imgcol" title="LindyLouMac"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1224346292p2/117720.jpg" alt="LindyLouMac" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/22911251?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 25, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/117720-lindyloumac" class="user" title="LindyLouMac">LindyLouMac</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/15104.Blackberry_Wine" title="Paperback 9780552998000" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer22911251">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12660418956281418559">Although I have had the majority of Joanne Harris's previous novels on my bookshelves for a number of years, so far I have only read Chocolat, Coastliners and Gentleman and Players. Now having just finished Blackberry Wine I intend to rectify this and catch up by reading the rest as soon as possible. So far she has proved to be for me a riveting storyteller, somehow making the locations and characters leap from the page. Her descriptions of food and wine so good that you feel you can smell and t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12660418956281418559">Although I have had the majority of Joanne Harris's previous novels on my bookshelves for a number of years, so far I have only read Chocolat, Coastliners and Gentleman and Players. Now having just finished Blackberry Wine I intend to rectify this and catch up by reading the rest as soon as possible. So far she has proved to be for me a riveting storyteller, somehow making the locations and characters leap from the page. Her descriptions of food and wine so good that you feel you can smell and taste them. I finished this with a glass of wine sitting in the garden this evening and felt transported to Lansquenet, which was also the location for Chocolat. I believe also that some characters reappear in The Lollipop Shoes, receiving a copy of this recently as a gift is the inspiration to read the rest of her novels. <br /><br />In Blackberry Wine the narrator is a bottle of wine `Fleurie 1962' unfolding the tale of Jay Mackintosh as a boy in 1975 and an adult in 1999, when he impulsively buys an old house in Lanssquenet, France. <br />In two interlinking narratives we learn how the time he spent as a teenager in Kirby Monckton with his friend an old man Joe, has a subconscious effect on his 1999 choices. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12660418956281418559">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a href="/review/list/3034846-melanti?shelf=e-book" class="actionLinkLite">e-book</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1038005935">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7499147492195144986">I was describing this book to a friend earlier today and she summed the plot up as being "Office Space with a magic bottle of wine instead of an occupational hypnotherapist." And she's certainly right!<br /><br />It's magical realism, of course, and a bit darker than Harris's <em>Chocolat</em> but not as dark as Alice Hoffman's work. And while set in the same town as <em>Chocolat</em>, it's not a direct sequel.<br /><br />There's a fair bit of whimsy to the book as well. A handful of chapters are narrated by a bottle of wine that's sitt</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7499147492195144986">I was describing this book to a friend earlier today and she summed the plot up as being "Office Space with a magic bottle of wine instead of an occupational hypnotherapist." And she's certainly right!<br /><br />It's magical realism, of course, and a bit darker than Harris's <em>Chocolat</em> but not as dark as Alice Hoffman's work. And while set in the same town as <em>Chocolat</em>, it's not a direct sequel.<br /><br />There's a fair bit of whimsy to the book as well. A handful of chapters are narrated by a bottle of wine that's sitting in the cellar waiting for its turn to share its memories. I'm not sure those chapters entirely mesh with the more prosaic third person chapters, but I appreciated the whimsy nonetheless.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5755941775209772599">It took me a while to get into this book, but by the end I really loved it. A feel-good book about a person having an internal crisis and his journey to a better place. We have all been there, but what makes this a beautiful story is how this man found himself in the unlikeliest of places. <br /><br />I think the moral is that we need to be open to anything if we are going to succeed in life, but that also means having the wherewithal to eliminate unnecessary things from our lives and know when something is</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5755941775209772599">It took me a while to get into this book, but by the end I really loved it. A feel-good book about a person having an internal crisis and his journey to a better place. We have all been there, but what makes this a beautiful story is how this man found himself in the unlikeliest of places. <br /><br />I think the moral is that we need to be open to anything if we are going to succeed in life, but that also means having the wherewithal to eliminate unnecessary things from our lives and know when something is not good for us.<br /><br />If you want to read a beautifully worded, touching story about a regular person not unlike yourself, this just might be the book for you.</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8268650167475659001">S?-i spui unui iubitor de licori selecte c? “vinul vorbe?te” pare s? fie un lucru de la sine în?eles (Joanne Harris sugereaz? chiar, în debutul romanului s?u, c? de fapt oricine ?tie asta – de la oracolul de la col?ul str?zii ?i pân? la prostul cel nebun). Pe de o parte, vinul vorbe?te direct degust?torului – o poveste despre recoltele fabuloase, despre timpul petrecut prin butoaie bine p?strate ?i despre aromele florale sau fructate ale unor veri de neuitat. Pe de alt? parte vinul este ?i un bun ventriloc - tot el vorbe?te ,prin milioanele de voci ale tuturor celor care îl degust?, despre planuri splendide, iubiri tragice ?i tr?d?ri teribile dezvaluite în momente decisive. Acest martor t?cut, nelipsit îns? de spirit de observa?ie, din sticlele bine pastrate, care conserv? de fapt fragmente de eternitate ?i e capabil s? r?scoleasc? cele mai intense ?i profunde tr?iri prime?te voce în splendida crea?ie a Joannei Harris. C?ci romanul prozatoarei britanice este o poveste spus? din perspectiva unei sticle de vin. Nu e vorba de orice vin totu?i, ci de un Fleurie din 1962, anul na?terii personajului principal. Un narator original vinul vioi, limbut, voios ?i pu?in obraznic are puterea nu doar de a dep?na povestea ci ?i de a schimba destinul personajelor la momentul potrivit. <div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_846913925">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/846913925" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5642580-christine-blachford" class="left imgcol" title="Christine Blachford"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442602635p2/5642580.jpg" alt="Christine Blachford" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/846913925?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 06, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5642580-christine-blachford" class="user" title="Christine Blachford">Christine Blachford</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer846913925">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8802813142648034641">Jay wrote a book about his childhood neighbour and influential friend Joe. Now he’s being pushed to write a sequel, so he moves to rural France to escape the pressure. With the quiet solitude around him, he finds inspiration to write but then finds he likes this French world far more than his previous existence.<br /><br />Jay seems to be a bit of a weak-willed and weak-minded character, but as we go through the book and learn things that happened in his childhood, it’s great to get a better understanding o</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8802813142648034641">Jay wrote a book about his childhood neighbour and influential friend Joe. Now he’s being pushed to write a sequel, so he moves to rural France to escape the pressure. With the quiet solitude around him, he finds inspiration to write but then finds he likes this French world far more than his previous existence.<br /><br />Jay seems to be a bit of a weak-willed and weak-minded character, but as we go through the book and learn things that happened in his childhood, it’s great to get a better understanding of what makes him tick. It also makes his growth as a person that much more rewarding, for the reader as well.<br /><br />I love that the village he has gone to is the same one that featured in Chocolat, with some of the same supporting characters and locations. Vianne Rocher has long gone, though. Oh, and Clopette is the best name ever. Okay, it’s for a goat, but still.<br /><br />What I have yet to mention is that the story is told from the perspective of a bottle of wine, which sounds crazy. As the story progresses, you forget who is telling the tale, though, and it just becomes another third person novel. Harris excels, as she always does, with her descriptions. I could feel the heat of summer and taste the scent of berries on the air. I preferred Chocolat, but this is a great sort of sequel.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8802813142648034641">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_7015862">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/7015862?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 09, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/122647-sarah-sammis" class="user" title="Sarah Sammis">Sarah Sammis</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer7015862">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15357279707686732044">Blackberry Wine is sickeningly sweet in its sentimentality but it does score points for having a unique narrator. The flashbacks to Pog Hill distract from the present day story. The book is tighter and more compelling a read when those chapters are skipped. When the story finally moves away from Jay's fond memories of how great Joe was and goes to the mystery of Jay's neighbor and her daughter Rosa the story hits its stride. I wish it had focused more on them and less on "Jackapple Joe."</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1034494096">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1034494096" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/11565234-carlin" class="left imgcol" title="Carlin"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Carlin" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1034494096?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 26, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/11565234-carlin" class="user" title="Carlin">Carlin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/11565234-carlin?shelf=on-kindle" class="actionLinkLite">on-kindle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1034494096">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer582357317098190150">This book, by the author of Chocolat (one of my all time favorite novels and movies), captured me from the very first page. The story of Jay Macintosh shifts back and forth between the present and the past, especially three summers during his adolescence when he met Joe Cox, an old man who had an enormous influence on Jay's life. Jay is a writer, whose first novel (about Joe) was a great success but who has been unable to write anything worth publishing for 15 years. He moves from London to a sm</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText582357317098190150">This book, by the author of Chocolat (one of my all time favorite novels and movies), captured me from the very first page. The story of Jay Macintosh shifts back and forth between the present and the past, especially three summers during his adolescence when he met Joe Cox, an old man who had an enormous influence on Jay's life. Jay is a writer, whose first novel (about Joe) was a great success but who has been unable to write anything worth publishing for 15 years. He moves from London to a small town in France where he has purchased a house, impulsively and sight unseen, to reinvent his life and to reawaken his writing career. The neighbors and villagers he meets inspire his new book and their stories find their way into the story. Old Joe magically appears in Jay's new home with advice and support. As in Chocolat, the magic plays an important role but never seems unrealistic in the context of the story. There is romance and intrigue, but the primary story of the relationship between Joe and Jay is the meat of the novel. I loved this book and plan to read more by this author (including two sequels to Chocolat).</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="582357317098190150">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WHF3zUwoyPLuUW1d7nkuXgiEcbXfzZdtEnVpQylTD9E9pUgevvrcCGKJGeaQGMjsQXOyrJYQ0Md4fGzR5cb5lA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oh8aX4863RZtToNtMqKcGZkehnhkiXIsyowaLcMhlDnHyyWMfejJ7OGW99ZMw3qr0OlFYS1UNYaghR+/D7RifA==')})
  }
//]]&gt;
</script>

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/9432.Joanne_Harris">About Joanne Harris</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/9432.Joanne_Harris"><img alt="9432" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1411031584p2/9432.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer2784142951156285730">Joanne Harris is an Anglo-French author, whose books include fourteen novels, two cookbooks and many short stories. Her work is extremely diverse, covering aspects of magic realism, suspense, historical fiction, mythology and fantasy. She has also written a DR WHO novella for the BBC, has scripted guest episodes for the game ZOMBIES, RUN!, and is currently engaged in a number of musical theatre pr</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2784142951156285730">Joanne Harris is an Anglo-French author, whose books include fourteen novels, two cookbooks and many short stories. Her work is extremely diverse, covering aspects of magic realism, suspense, historical fiction, mythology and fantasy. She has also written a DR WHO novella for the BBC, has scripted guest episodes for the game ZOMBIES, RUN!, and is currently engaged in a number of musical theatre projects as well as developing an original drama for television.<br />In 2000, her 1999 novel CHOCOLAT was adapted to the screen, starring Juliette Binoche and Johnny Depp. She is an honorary Fellow of St Catharine's College, Cambridge, and in 2013 was awarded an MBE by the Queen.<br />Her hobbies are listed in Who's Who as 'mooching, lounging, strutting, strumming, priest-baiting and quiet subversion'. She also spends too much time on Twitter; plays flute and bass guitar in a band first formed when she was 16; and works from a shed in her garden at her home in Yorkshire.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2784142951156285730">...more</a>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/9432.Joanne_Harris" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Joanne Harris...</a>
<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>
